Due to the short reads sequenced by the Illumina platform and a large number of repeat sequences, the total lengths of genome assembly (~736.66 Mb) and repetitive sequences (~456.57 Mb) are shorter than those in the previous genome assembly (~776.96 Mb and ~528.04 Mb, respectively)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Wu, Z. G. et al. De novo genome assembly of Oryza granulata reveals rapid genome expansion and adaptive evolution. Commun. Biol. 1, 84 (2018)." href="/articles/s41597-020-0470-2#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d4230e2495">11</a></sup> (Online-only Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41597-020-0470-2#Tab10">1</a>). This may be attributed to the ~21 × PacBio data overcoming the above-mentioned difficulties to some extent, resulting in the assembly of an additional portion of repetitive sequences. However, we obtained fewer scaffolds but a longer scaffold N50 compared to those in the previous genome assembly<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Wu, Z. G. et al. De novo genome assembly of Oryza granulata reveals rapid genome expansion and adaptive evolution. Commun. Biol. 1, 84 (2018)." href="/articles/s41597-020-0470-2#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d4230e2502">11</a></sup>. We predicted 40,131 protein-coding genes and observed that the gene and ncRNA annotations were somewhat better than those for the previous genome assembly (Online-only Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="table anchor" href="/articles/s41597-020-0470-2#Tab10">1</a>). This was also evidenced by the evaluation using BUSCO, showing that 1,390 genes (~96.53%) were completely identified, which is somewhat better than the number for the previous genome assembly<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Wu, Z. G. et al. De novo genome assembly of Oryza granulata reveals rapid genome expansion and adaptive evolution. Commun. Biol. 1, 84 (2018)." href="/articles/s41597-020-0470-2#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d4230e2509">11</a></sup>. Thus, the newly released genome assembly, which has good continuity and integrity, is comparable to other sequenced <i>Oryza</i> genomes.</p></div></div></section>
                

                <section aria-labelledby="code-availability" data-title="Code availability"><div class="c-article-section" id="code-availability-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="code-availability">Code availability</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="code-availability-content">
              
              <p>The sequence data were generated using the software provided by the sequencing platform manufacturer and processed with commands provided for the public software cited in the manuscript. No custom computer code was generated in this work. The following bioinformatic tools and versions were used to generate all results as described in the main text. Default parameters were used if not stated.</p>
              <p>1. CellQuest version 5.1.</p>
              <p>2. GCE (Genome Characteristics Estimation) version 1.0.0 was used to estimate genome size, ftp://ftp.genomics.org.cn/pub/gce/.</p>
              <p>3. ALLPATHS-LG version 48894 was used for genome assembly, <a href="http://software.broadinstitute.org/allpaths-lg/blog/">http://software.broadinstitute.org/allpaths-lg/blog/</a>.</p>
              <p>4. SSPACE version 3.0 was used for genome assembly scaffolding, <a href="https://www.baseclear.com/services/bioinformatics/basetools/sspace-standard/">https://www.baseclear.com/services/bioinformatics/basetools/sspace-standard/</a>.</p>
              <p>5. GapCloser version 1.12 was used to fill the gaps between scaffolds, <a href="http://soap.genomics.org.cn/about.html">http://soap.genomics.org.cn/about.html</a>.</p>
              <p>6. BWA (Burrows-Wheeler Aligner) version 0.7.15 was used for short read mapping, <a href="https://github.com/lh3/bwa/">https://github.com/lh3/bwa/</a>.</p>
              <p>7. BUSCO (Benchmarking Universal Single-Copy Orthologs) was used to check the completeness of the genome assembly, with coverage ≥ 90% and identity ≥ 90% parameters, <a href="https://gitlab.com/ezlab/busco/">https://gitlab.com/ezlab/busco/</a>.</p>
              <p>8. Trinity version v2.0.6 was used to assemble the RNA sequencing reads, <a href="https://github.com/trinityrnaseq/trinityrnaseq">https://github.com/trinityrnaseq/trinityrnaseq</a>.</p>
              <p>9. GMAP version 2014-10-2 was used to map the assembled transcripts to the genome sequence with coverage ≥ 90% and identity ≥ 90% parameters, <a href="http://research-pub.gene.com/gmap">http://research-pub.gene.com/gmap</a>.</p>
              <p>10 LACHESIS was used for ultra-long-range scaffolding with Hi-C data with CLUSTER_N = 12, CLUSTER_MIN_RE_SITES = 300, CLUSTER_MAX_LINK_DENSITY = 8, ORDER_MIN_N_RES_IN_TRUNK = 100, and ORDER_MIN_N_RES_IN_SHREDS = 10 parameters, <a href="http://shendurelab.github.io/LACHESIS/">http://shendurelab.github.io/LACHESIS/</a>.</p>
              <p>11. RepeatMasker version 4.0.3 was used to mask the repeat sequences in the genome, <a href="http://repeatmasker.org/">http://repeatmasker.org/</a>.</p>
              <p>12. Augustus version 2.7 was used for <i>de novo</i> gene prediction, <a href="http://augustus.gobics.de/">http://augustus.gobics.de/</a>.</p>
              <p>13. SNAP version 2006-07-28 was used for <i>de novo</i> gene prediction, <a href="https://github.com/KorfLab/SNAP">https://github.com/KorfLab/SNAP</a>.</p>
              <p>14. Exonerate version 2.2.0 was used to align proteins to the genome sequence, <a href="https://www.ebi.ac.uk/~guy/exonerate/">https://www.ebi.ac.uk/~guy/exonerate/</a>.</p>
              <p>15. GeneWise version 2-2-0 was used to predict gene structure using similar protein sequences, <a href="http://www.ebi.ac.uk/~birney/wise2">http://www.ebi.ac.uk/~birney/wise2</a>.</p>
              <p>16. GenBlastA version 1.0.1 was used to link the high-scoring pairs (HSPs), <a href="http://genome.sfu.ca/genblast/download.html">http://genome.sfu.ca/genblast/download.html</a>.</p>
              <p>17. PASA (Program to Assemble Spliced Alignments) was used to exploit gene structure using transcripts, <a href="http://pasapipeline.github.io/">http://pasapipeline.github.io/</a>.</p>
              <p>18. EVidenceModeler (EVM) version 1.1.1 was used to combine gene predictions generated from different methods into consensus gene structures, <a href="http://evidencemodeler.github.io/">http://evidencemodeler.github.io/</a>.</p>
              <p>19. BLAST version 2.2.28 was used to find regions of local similarity between sequences, <a href="https://blast.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/Blast.cgi/">https://blast.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/Blast.cgi/</a>.</p>
              <p>20. KEGG (Kyoto Encyclopedia of Genes and Genomes), <a href="https://www.kegg.jp/">https://www.kegg.jp/</a>.</p>
              <p>21. Pfam database: <a href="http://pfam.xfam.org/">http://pfam.xfam.org/</a>.</p>
              <p>22. Blast2GO: <a href="https://www.blast2go.com/">https://www.blast2go.com/</a>.</p>
              <p>23. The tRNAscan-SE algorithm (version 1.23) was used for the identification of tRNA genes, <a href="http://lowelab.ucsc.edu/tRNAscan-SE">http://lowelab.ucsc.edu/tRNAscan-SE</a>.</p>
              <p>24. The RNAmmer algorithm was used for the identification of rRNA genes, <a href="http://www.cbs.dtu.dk/services/RNAmmer/">http://www.cbs.dtu.dk/services/RNAmmer/</a>.</p>
              <p>25. Snoscan version 1.0 was used for the identification of snoRNA genes, <a href="http://lowelab.ucsc.edu/snoscan/">http://lowelab.ucsc.edu/snoscan/</a>.</p>
              <p>26. INFERNAL version 1.1.2 was used for the identification of snRNA genes, <a href="http://eddylab.org/infernal/">http://eddylab.org/infernal/</a>.</p>
              <p>27. Rfam database release 9.1, rfam.xfam.org/.</p>
              <p>28. miRBase release 21, <a href="http://www.mirbase.org/">www.mirbase.org/</a>.</p>
              <p>29. psRNATarget server; parameters: maximum expectation = 3.0, length for complementary scoring = 20 bp, target accessibility – allowed maximum energy to unpair the target site = 25.0, flanking length around the target site for target accessibility analysis: 17 bp upstream and 13 bp downstream, and range of central mismatch leading to translational inhibition = 9~11 bp, <a href="http://plantgrn.noble.org/psRNATarget/">http://plantgrn.noble.org/psRNATarget/</a>.</p>
              <p>30 Rice Genome Annotation Project Database, <a href="http://rice.plantbiology.msu.edu/">http://rice.plantbiology.msu.edu/</a>.</p>
              <p>31. agriGO server, <a href="http://bioinfor.cau.edu.cn/agiGO/">http://bioinfor.cau.edu.cn/agiGO/</a>.</p>
              <p>32. BlastKOALA, <a href="http://kegg.jp/blastkoala/">http://kegg.jp/blastkoala/</a>.</p>
              <p>33. Repbase TE library (version released on January 31, 2014).</p>
              <p>34. RepeatProteinMask, <a href="http://www.repeatmasker.org/RepeatProteinMask.html">http://www.repeatmasker.org/RepeatProteinMask.html</a>.</p>
              <p>35. RepeatModeler version 1.0.10 was used for <i>de novo</i> repeat family identification and modelling, <a href="http://www.repeatmasker.org/RepeatModeler/">http://www.repeatmasker.org/RepeatModeler/</a>.</p>
              <p>36. RECON version 1.08.</p>
              <p>37. RepeatScout version 1.0.5.</p>
              <p>38. LTR_STRUC was used for the identification of LTR retrotransposons, <a href="http://www.mcdonaldlab.biology.gatech.edu/ltr_struc.htm">http://www.mcdonaldlab.biology.gatech.edu/ltr_struc.htm</a>.</p>
              <p>39. ClustalW was used to perform multiple sequence alignment, <a href="https://www.genome.jp/tools-bin/clustalw">https://www.genome.jp/tools-bin/clustalw</a>.</p>
              <p>40. <i>Gypsy</i> Database (GyDB), <a href="http://gydb.org/">http://gydb.org/</a>.</p>
              <p>41. Tandem Repeat Finder (TRF) version 4.07b was used to find the tandem repeats in the genome with the parameters Match = 2, Mismatch = 7, Delta = 7, PM = 80, PI = 10, Minscore = 50, and MaxPeriod = 12, <a href="https://tandem.bu.edu/trf/trf.html">https://tandem.bu.edu/trf/trf.html</a>.</p>
              <p>42. RepeatMasker version 4.0.3 was used to mask the repeat sequences in the genome with the parameter -noint, <a href="http://www.repeatmasker.org">http://www.repeatmasker.org</a>.</p>
              <p>43. The MISA (MIcroSAtellite) identification tool was used for the identification and localization of microsatellites, <a href="http://pgrc.ipk-gatersleben.de/misa/">http://pgrc.ipk-gatersleben.de/misa/</a>.</p>
              <p>44. Trimmomatic version 0.33 was used for the quality filtering of sequencing reads, <a href="http://www.usadellab.org/cms/index.php?page=trimmomatic">http://www.usadellab.org/cms/index.php?page=trimmomatic</a>.</p>
            </div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Bib1" data-title="References"><div class="c-article-section" id="Bib1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Bib1">References</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Bib1-content"><div data-container-section="references"><ol class="c-article-references"><li class="c-article-references__item js-c-reading-companion-references-item" itemprop="citation" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle"><meta itemprop="author" content="M.     <a data-track="click" data-track-action="outbound reference" data-track-label="link" href="/articles/cas-redirect/1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BD38XivVSqtrw%253D" aria-label="View reference 9 on CAS">CAS</a>

    <a data-track="click" data-track-action="outbound reference" data-track-label="link" aria-label="Search for reference 9 on Google Scholar" href="http://scholar.google.com/scholar_lookup?&amp;title=A%20draft%20sequence%20of%20the%20rice%20genome%20%28Oryza%20sativa%20L.%20ssp.%20japonica%29&amp;journal=Science&amp;volume=296&amp;pages=92-100&amp;publication_year=2002&amp;author=Goff%2CSA">
                    Google Scholar</a> 
                </p></li><li class="c-article-references__item js-c-reading-companion-references-item" itemprop="citation" itemscope="itemscope" itemtype="http://schema.org/ScholarlyArticle"><meta itemprop="author" content="B.                     id="authors-2">
